<div class="markdown-heading" dir="auto"><h2 tabindex="-1" class="heading-element" dir="auto">Our approach to prompting</h2><a id="user-content-our-approach-to-prompting" class="anchor" aria-label="Permalink: Our approach to prompting" href="#our-approach-to-prompting"><svg class="octicon octicon-link" viewBox="0 0 16 16" version="1.1" width="16" height="16" aria-hidden="true"><path d="m7.775 3.275 1.25-1.25a3.5 3.5 0 1 1 4.95 4.95l-2.5 2.5a3.5 3.5 0 0 1-4.95 0 .751.751 0 0 1 .018-1.042.751.751 0 0 1 1.042-.018 1.998 1.998 0 0 0 2.83 0l2.5-2.5a2.002 2.002 0 0 0-2.83-2.83l-1.25 1.25a.751.751 0 0 1-1.042-.018.751.751 0 0 1-.018-1.042Zm-4.69 9.64a1.998 1.998 0 0 0 2.83 0l1.25-1.25a.751.751 0 0 1 1.042.018.751.751 0 0 1 .018 1.042l-1.25 1.25a3.5 3.5 0 1 1-4.95-4.95l2.5-2.5a3.5 3.5 0 0 1 4.95 0 .751.751 0 0 1-.018 1.042.751.751 0 0 1-1.042.018 1.998 1.998 0 0 0-2.83 0l-2.5 2.5a1.998 1.998 0 0 0 0 2.83Z"></path></svg></a></div>
<p dir="auto">Fabric <em>Patterns</em> are different than most prompts you'll see.</p>
<ul dir="auto">
<li><strong>First, we use <code>Markdown</code> to help ensure maximum readability and editability</strong>. This not only helps the creator make a good one, but also anyone who wants to deeply understand what it does. <em>Importantly, this also includes the AI you're sending it to!</em></li>
</ul>
<p dir="auto">Here's an example of a Fabric Pattern.</p>
<div class="highlight highlight-source-shell notranslate position-relative overflow-auto" dir="auto" data-snippet-clipboard-copy-content="https://github.com/danielmiessler/fabric/blob/main/patterns/extract_wisdom/system.md"><pre>https://github.com/danielmiessler/fabric/blob/main/patterns/extract_wisdom/system.md</pre></div>
<p dir="auto"><a target="_blank" rel="noopener noreferrer" href="https://github.com/danielmiessler/fabric/assets/50654/b910c551-9263-405f-9735-71ca69bbab6d"><img width="1461" alt="pattern-example" src="https://github.com/danielmiessler/fabric/assets/50654/b910c551-9263-405f-9735-71ca69bbab6d" style="max-width: 100%;"></a></p>
<ul dir="auto">
<li>
<p dir="auto"><strong>Next, we are extremely clear in our instructions</strong>, and we use the Markdown structure to emphasize what we want the AI to do, and in what order.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p dir="auto"><strong>And finally, we tend to use the System section of the prompt almost exclusively</strong>. In over a year of being heads-down with this stuff, we've just seen more efficacy from doing that. If that changes, or we're shown data that says otherwise, we will adjust.</p>
</li>
</ul>
<div class="markdown-heading" dir="auto"><h2 tabindex="-1" class="heading-element" dir="auto">Examples</h2><a id="user-content-examples" class="anchor" aria-label="Permalink: Examples" href="#examples"><svg class="octicon octicon-link" viewBox="0 0 16 16" version="1.1" width="16" height="16" aria-hidden="true"><path d="m7.775 3.275 1.25-1.25a3.5 3.5 0 1 1 4.95 4.95l-2.5 2.5a3.5 3.5 0 0 1-4.95 0 .751.751 0 0 1 .018-1.042.751.751 0 0 1 1.042-.018 1.998 1.998 0 0 0 2.83 0l2.5-2.5a2.002 2.002 0 0 0-2.83-2.83l-1.25 1.25a.751.751 0 0 1-1.042-.018.751.751 0 0 1-.018-1.042Zm-4.69 9.64a1.998 1.998 0 0 0 2.83 0l1.25-1.25a.751.751 0 0 1 1.042.018.751.751 0 0 1 .018 1.042l-1.25 1.25a3.5 3.5 0 1 1-4.95-4.95l2.5-2.5a3.5 3.5 0 0 1 4.95 0 .751.751 0 0 1-.018 1.042.751.751 0 0 1-1.042.018 1.998 1.998 0 0 0-2.83 0l-2.5 2.5a1.998 1.998 0 0 0 0 2.83Z"></path></svg></a></div>
<blockquote>
<p dir="auto">The following examples use the macOS <code>pbpaste</code> to paste from the clipboard. See the <a href="#pbpaste">pbpaste</a> section below for Windows and Linux alternatives.</p>
</blockquote>
<p dir="auto">Now let's look at some things you can do with Fabric.</p>
<ol dir="auto">
<li>
<p dir="auto">Run the <code>summarize</code> Pattern based on input from <code>stdin</code>. In this case, the body of an article.</p>
<div class="highlight highlight-source-shell notranslate position-relative overflow-auto" dir="auto" data-snippet-clipboard-copy-content="pbpaste | fabric --pattern summarize"><pre>pbpaste <span class="pl-k">|</span> fabric --pattern summarize</pre></div>
</li>
<li>
<p dir="auto">Run the <code>analyze_claims</code> Pattern with the <code>--stream</code> option to get immediate and streaming results.</p>
<div class="highlight highlight-source-shell notranslate position-relative overflow-auto" dir="auto" data-snippet-clipboard-copy-content="pbpaste | fabric --stream --pattern analyze_claims"><pre>pbpaste <span class="pl-k">|</span> fabric --stream --pattern analyze_claims</pre></div>
</li>
<li>
<p dir="auto">Run the <code>extract_wisdom</code> Pattern with the <code>--stream</code> option to get immediate and streaming results from any      Youtube video (much like in the original introduction video).</p>
<div class="highlight highlight-source-shell notranslate position-relative overflow-auto" dir="auto" data-snippet-clipboard-copy-content="fabric -y &quot;https://youtube.com/watch?v=uXs-zPc63kM&quot; --stream --pattern extract_wisdom"><pre>fabric -y <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">"</span>https://youtube.com/watch?v=uXs-zPc63kM<span class="pl-pds">"</span></span> --stream --pattern extract_wisdom</pre></div>
</li>
<li>
<p dir="auto">Create patterns- you must create a .md file with the pattern and save it to <code>~/.config/fabric/patterns/[yourpatternname]</code>.</p>
</li>
<li>
<p dir="auto">Run a <code>analyze_claims</code> pattern on a website. Fabric uses Jina AI to scrape the URL into markdown format before sending it to the model.</p>
<div class="highlight highlight-source-shell notranslate position-relative overflow-auto" dir="auto" data-snippet-clipboard-copy-content="fabric -u https://github.com/danielmiessler/fabric/ -p analyze_claims"><pre>fabric -u https://github.com/danielmiessler/fabric/ -p analyze_claims</pre></div>
</li>
</ol>
<div class="markdown-heading" dir="auto"><h2 tabindex="-1" class="heading-element" dir="auto">Just use the Patterns</h2><a id="user-content-just-use-the-patterns" class="anchor" aria-label="Permalink: Just use the Patterns" href="#just-use-the-patterns"><svg class="octicon octicon-link" viewBox="0 0 16 16" version="1.1" width="16" height="16" aria-hidden="true"><path d="m7.775 3.275 1.25-1.25a3.5 3.5 0 1 1 4.95 4.95l-2.5 2.5a3.5 3.5 0 0 1-4.95 0 .751.751 0 0 1 .018-1.042.751.751 0 0 1 1.042-.018 1.998 1.998 0 0 0 2.83 0l2.5-2.5a2.002 2.002 0 0 0-2.83-2.83l-1.25 1.25a.751.751 0 0 1-1.042-.018.751.751 0 0 1-.018-1.042Zm-4.69 9.64a1.998 1.998 0 0 0 2.83 0l1.25-1.25a.751.751 0 0 1 1.042.018.751.751 0 0 1 .018 1.042l-1.25 1.25a3.5 3.5 0 1 1-4.95-4.95l2.5-2.5a3.5 3.5 0 0 1 4.95 0 .751.751 0 0 1-.018 1.042.751.751 0 0 1-1.042.018 1.998 1.998 0 0 0-2.83 0l-2.5 2.5a1.998 1.998 0 0 0 0 2.83Z"></path></svg></a></div>
<p dir="auto"><a target="_blank" rel="noopener noreferrer" href="https://github.com/danielmiessler/fabric/assets/50654/9186a044-652b-4673-89f7-71cf066f32d8"><img width="1173" alt="fabric-patterns-screenshot" src="https://github.com/danielmiessler/fabric/assets/50654/9186a044-652b-4673-89f7-71cf066f32d8" style="max-width: 100%;"></a></p>
<br>
<br>
<p dir="auto">If you're not looking to do anything fancy, and you just want a lot of great prompts, you can navigate to the <a href="https://github.com/danielmiessler/fabric/tree/main/data/patterns"><code>/patterns</code></a> directory and start exploring!</p>
<p dir="auto">We hope that if you used nothing else from Fabric, the Patterns by themselves will make the project useful.</p>
<p dir="auto">You can use any of the Patterns you see there in any AI application that you have, whether that's ChatGPT or some other app or website. Our plan and prediction is that people will soon be sharing many more than those we've published, and they will be way better than ours.</p>
<p dir="auto">The wisdom of crowds for the win.</p>
<div class="markdown-heading" dir="auto"><h3 tabindex="-1" class="heading-element" dir="auto">Prompt Strategies</h3><a id="user-content-prompt-strategies" class="anchor" aria-label="Permalink: Prompt Strategies" href="#prompt-strategies"><svg class="octicon octicon-link" viewBox="0 0 16 16" version="1.1" width="16" height="16" aria-hidden="true"><path d="m7.775 3.275 1.25-1.25a3.5 3.5 0 1 1 4.95 4.95l-2.5 2.5a3.5 3.5 0 0 1-4.95 0 .751.751 0 0 1 .018-1.042.751.751 0 0 1 1.042-.018 1.998 1.998 0 0 0 2.83 0l2.5-2.5a2.002 2.002 0 0 0-2.83-2.83l-1.25 1.25a.751.751 0 0 1-1.042-.018.751.751 0 0 1-.018-1.042Zm-4.69 9.64a1.998 1.998 0 0 0 2.83 0l1.25-1.25a.751.751 0 0 1 1.042.018.751.751 0 0 1 .018 1.042l-1.25 1.25a3.5 3.5 0 1 1-4.95-4.95l2.5-2.5a3.5 3.5 0 0 1 4.95 0 .751.751 0 0 1-.018 1.042.751.751 0 0 1-1.042.018 1.998 1.998 0 0 0-2.83 0l-2.5 2.5a1.998 1.998 0 0 0 0 2.83Z"></path></svg></a></div>
<p dir="auto">Fabric also implements prompt strategies like "Chain of Thought" or "Chain of Draft" which can
be used in addition to the basic patterns.</p>
<p dir="auto">See the <a href="https://arxiv.org/pdf/2502.18600" rel="nofollow">Thinking Faster by Writing Less</a> paper and
the <a href="https://learnprompting.org/docs/advanced/thought_generation/introduction" rel="nofollow">Thought Generation section of Learn Prompting</a> for examples of prompt strategies.</p>
<p dir="auto">Each strategy is available as a small <code>json</code> file in the <a href="https://github.com/danielmiessler/fabric/tree/main/data/strategies"><code>/strategies</code></a> directory.</p>
<p dir="auto">The prompt modification of the strategy is applied to the system prompt and passed on to the
LLM in the chat session.</p>
<p dir="auto">Use <code>fabric -S</code> and select the option to install the strategies in your <code>~/.config/fabric</code> directory.</p>
<div class="markdown-heading" dir="auto"><h2 tabindex="-1" class="heading-element" dir="auto">Custom Patterns</h2><a id="user-content-custom-patterns" class="anchor" aria-label="Permalink: Custom Patterns" href="#custom-patterns"><svg class="octicon octicon-link" viewBox="0 0 16 16" version="1.1" width="16" height="16" aria-hidden="true"><path d="m7.775 3.275 1.25-1.25a3.5 3.5 0 1 1 4.95 4.95l-2.5 2.5a3.5 3.5 0 0 1-4.95 0 .751.751 0 0 1 .018-1.042.751.751 0 0 1 1.042-.018 1.998 1.998 0 0 0 2.83 0l2.5-2.5a2.002 2.002 0 0 0-2.83-2.83l-1.25 1.25a.751.751 0 0 1-1.042-.018.751.751 0 0 1-.018-1.042Zm-4.69 9.64a1.998 1.998 0 0 0 2.83 0l1.25-1.25a.751.751 0 0 1 1.042.018.751.751 0 0 1 .018 1.042l-1.25 1.25a3.5 3.5 0 1 1-4.95-4.95l2.5-2.5a3.5 3.5 0 0 1 4.95 0 .751.751 0 0 1-.018 1.042.751.751 0 0 1-1.042.018 1.998 1.998 0 0 0-2.83 0l-2.5 2.5a1.998 1.998 0 0 0 0 2.83Z"></path></svg></a></div>
<p dir="auto">You may want to use Fabric to create your own custom Patterns—but not share them with others. No problem!</p>
<p dir="auto">Fabric now supports a dedicated custom patterns directory that keeps your personal patterns separate from the built-in ones. This means your custom patterns won't be overwritten when you update Fabric's built-in patterns.</p>
<div class="markdown-heading" dir="auto"><h3 tabindex="-1" class="heading-element" dir="auto">Setting Up Custom Patterns</h3><a id="user-content-setting-up-custom-patterns" class="anchor" aria-label="Permalink: Setting Up Custom Patterns" href="#setting-up-custom-patterns"><svg class="octicon octicon-link" viewBox="0 0 16 16" version="1.1" width="16" height="16" aria-hidden="true"><path d="m7.775 3.275 1.25-1.25a3.5 3.5 0 1 1 4.95 4.95l-2.5 2.5a3.5 3.5 0 0 1-4.95 0 .751.751 0 0 1 .018-1.042.751.751 0 0 1 1.042-.018 1.998 1.998 0 0 0 2.83 0l2.5-2.5a2.002 2.002 0 0 0-2.83-2.83l-1.25 1.25a.751.751 0 0 1-1.042-.018.751.751 0 0 1-.018-1.042Zm-4.69 9.64a1.998 1.998 0 0 0 2.83 0l1.25-1.25a.751.751 0 0 1 1.042.018.751.751 0 0 1 .018 1.042l-1.25 1.25a3.5 3.5 0 1 1-4.95-4.95l2.5-2.5a3.5 3.5 0 0 1 4.95 0 .751.751 0 0 1-.018 1.042.751.751 0 0 1-1.042.018 1.998 1.998 0 0 0-2.83 0l-2.5 2.5a1.998 1.998 0 0 0 0 2.83Z"></path></svg></a></div>
<ol dir="auto">
<li>
<p dir="auto">Run the Fabric setup:</p>
<div class="highlight highlight-source-shell notranslate position-relative overflow-auto" dir="auto" data-snippet-clipboard-copy-content="fabric --setup"><pre>fabric --setup</pre></div>
</li>
<li>
<p dir="auto">Select the "Custom Patterns" option from the Tools menu and enter your desired directory path (e.g., <code>~/my-custom-patterns</code>)</p>
</li>
<li>
<p dir="auto">Fabric will automatically create the directory if it does not exist.</p>
</li>
</ol>
<div class="markdown-heading" dir="auto"><h3 tabindex="-1" class="heading-element" dir="auto">Using Custom Patterns</h3><a id="user-content-using-custom-patterns" class="anchor" aria-label="Permalink: Using Custom Patterns" href="#using-custom-patterns"><svg class="octicon octicon-link" viewBox="0 0 16 16" version="1.1" width="16" height="16" aria-hidden="true"><path d="m7.775 3.275 1.25-1.25a3.5 3.5 0 1 1 4.95 4.95l-2.5 2.5a3.5 3.5 0 0 1-4.95 0 .751.751 0 0 1 .018-1.042.751.751 0 0 1 1.042-.018 1.998 1.998 0 0 0 2.83 0l2.5-2.5a2.002 2.002 0 0 0-2.83-2.83l-1.25 1.25a.751.751 0 0 1-1.042-.018.751.751 0 0 1-.018-1.042Zm-4.69 9.64a1.998 1.998 0 0 0 2.83 0l1.25-1.25a.751.751 0 0 1 1.042.018.751.751 0 0 1 .018 1.042l-1.25 1.25a3.5 3.5 0 1 1-4.95-4.95l2.5-2.5a3.5 3.5 0 0 1 4.95 0 .751.751 0 0 1-.018 1.042.751.751 0 0 1-1.042.018 1.998 1.998 0 0 0-2.83 0l-2.5 2.5a1.998 1.998 0 0 0 0 2.83Z"></path></svg></a></div>
<ol dir="auto">
<li>
<p dir="auto">Create your custom pattern directory structure:</p>
<div class="highlight highlight-source-shell notranslate position-relative overflow-auto" dir="auto" data-snippet-clipboard-copy-content="mkdir -p ~/my-custom-patterns/my-analyzer"><pre>mkdir -p <span class="pl-k">~</span>/my-custom-patterns/my-analyzer</pre></div>
</li>
<li>
<p dir="auto">Create your pattern file</p>
<div class="highlight highlight-source-shell notranslate position-relative overflow-auto" dir="auto" data-snippet-clipboard-copy-content="echo &quot;You are an expert analyzer of ...&quot; &gt; ~/my-custom-patterns/my-analyzer/system.md"><pre><span class="pl-c1">echo</span> <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">"</span>You are an expert analyzer of ...<span class="pl-pds">"</span></span> <span class="pl-k">&gt;</span> <span class="pl-k">~</span>/my-custom-patterns/my-analyzer/system.md</pre></div>
</li>
<li>
<p dir="auto"><strong>Use your custom pattern:</strong></p>
<div class="highlight highlight-source-shell notranslate position-relative overflow-auto" dir="auto" data-snippet-clipboard-copy-content="fabric --pattern my-analyzer &quot;analyze this text&quot;"><pre>fabric --pattern my-analyzer <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">"</span>analyze this text<span class="pl-pds">"</span></span></pre></div>
</li>
</ol>
<div class="markdown-heading" dir="auto"><h3 tabindex="-1" class="heading-element" dir="auto">How It Works</h3><a id="user-content-how-it-works" class="anchor" aria-label="Permalink: How It Works" href="#how-it-works"><svg class="octicon octicon-link" viewBox="0 0 16 16" version="1.1" width="16" height="16" aria-hidden="true"><path d="m7.775 3.275 1.25-1.25a3.5 3.5 0 1 1 4.95 4.95l-2.5 2.5a3.5 3.5 0 0 1-4.95 0 .751.751 0 0 1 .018-1.042.751.751 0 0 1 1.042-.018 1.998 1.998 0 0 0 2.83 0l2.5-2.5a2.002 2.002 0 0 0-2.83-2.83l-1.25 1.25a.751.751 0 0 1-1.042-.018.751.751 0 0 1-.018-1.042Zm-4.69 9.64a1.998 1.998 0 0 0 2.83 0l1.25-1.25a.751.751 0 0 1 1.042.018.751.751 0 0 1 .018 1.042l-1.25 1.25a3.5 3.5 0 1 1-4.95-4.95l2.5-2.5a3.5 3.5 0 0 1 4.95 0 .751.751 0 0 1-.018 1.042.751.751 0 0 1-1.042.018 1.998 1.998 0 0 0-2.83 0l-2.5 2.5a1.998 1.998 0 0 0 0 2.83Z"></path></svg></a></div>
<ul dir="auto">
<li><strong>Priority System</strong>: Custom patterns take precedence over built-in patterns with the same name</li>
<li><strong>Seamless Integration</strong>: Custom patterns appear in <code>fabric --listpatterns</code> alongside built-in ones</li>
<li><strong>Update Safe</strong>: Your custom patterns are never affected by <code>fabric --updatepatterns</code></li>
<li><strong>Private by Default</strong>: Custom patterns remain private unless you explicitly share them</li>
</ul>
<p dir="auto">Your custom patterns are completely private and won't be affected by Fabric updates!</p>
<div class="markdown-heading" dir="auto"><h2 tabindex="-1" class="heading-element" dir="auto">Helper Apps</h2><a id="user-content-helper-apps" class="anchor" aria-label="Permalink: Helper Apps" href="#helper-apps"><svg class="octicon octicon-link" viewBox="0 0 16 16" version="1.1" width="16" height="16" aria-hidden="true"><path d="m7.775 3.275 1.25-1.25a3.5 3.5 0 1 1 4.95 4.95l-2.5 2.5a3.5 3.5 0 0 1-4.95 0 .751.751 0 0 1 .018-1.042.751.751 0 0 1 1.042-.018 1.998 1.998 0 0 0 2.83 0l2.5-2.5a2.002 2.002 0 0 0-2.83-2.83l-1.25 1.25a.751.751 0 0 1-1.042-.018.751.751 0 0 1-.018-1.042Zm-4.69 9.64a1.998 1.998 0 0 0 2.83 0l1.25-1.25a.751.751 0 0 1 1.042.018.751.751 0 0 1 .018 1.042l-1.25 1.25a3.5 3.5 0 1 1-4.95-4.95l2.5-2.5a3.5 3.5 0 0 1 4.95 0 .751.751 0 0 1-.018 1.042.751.751 0 0 1-1.042.018 1.998 1.998 0 0 0-2.83 0l-2.5 2.5a1.998 1.998 0 0 0 0 2.83Z"></path></svg></a></div>
<p dir="auto">Fabric also makes use of some core helper apps (tools) to make it easier to integrate with your various workflows. Here are some examples:</p>
<div class="markdown-heading" dir="auto"><h3 tabindex="-1" class="heading-element" dir="auto"><code>to_pdf</code></h3><a id="user-content-to_pdf" class="anchor" aria-label="Permalink: to_pdf" href="#to_pdf"><svg class="octicon octicon-link" viewBox="0 0 16 16" version="1.1" width="16" height="16" aria-hidden="true"><path d="m7.775 3.275 1.25-1.25a3.5 3.5 0 1 1 4.95 4.95l-2.5 2.5a3.5 3.5 0 0 1-4.95 0 .751.751 0 0 1 .018-1.042.751.751 0 0 1 1.042-.018 1.998 1.998 0 0 0 2.83 0l2.5-2.5a2.002 2.002 0 0 0-2.83-2.83l-1.25 1.25a.751.751 0 0 1-1.042-.018.751.751 0 0 1-.018-1.042Zm-4.69 9.64a1.998 1.998 0 0 0 2.83 0l1.25-1.25a.751.751 0 0 1 1.042.018.751.751 0 0 1 .018 1.042l-1.25 1.25a3.5 3.5 0 1 1-4.95-4.95l2.5-2.5a3.5 3.5 0 0 1 4.95 0 .751.751 0 0 1-.018 1.042.751.751 0 0 1-1.042.018 1.998 1.998 0 0 0-2.83 0l-2.5 2.5a1.998 1.998 0 0 0 0 2.83Z"></path></svg></a></div>
<p dir="auto"><code>to_pdf</code> is a helper command that converts LaTeX files to PDF format. You can use it like this:</p>
<div class="highlight highlight-source-shell notranslate position-relative overflow-auto" dir="auto" data-snippet-clipboard-copy-content="to_pdf input.tex"><pre>to_pdf input.tex</pre></div>
<p dir="auto">This will create a PDF file from the input LaTeX file in the same directory.</p>
<p dir="auto">You can also use it with stdin which works perfectly with the <code>write_latex</code> pattern:</p>
<div class="highlight highlight-source-shell notranslate position-relative overflow-auto" dir="auto" data-snippet-clipboard-copy-content="echo &quot;ai security primer&quot; | fabric --pattern write_latex | to_pdf"><pre><span class="pl-c1">echo</span> <span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">"</span>ai security primer<span class="pl-pds">"</span></span> <span class="pl-k">|</span> fabric --pattern write_latex <span class="pl-k">|</span> to_pdf</pre></div>
<p dir="auto">This will create a PDF file named <code>output.pdf</code> in the current directory.</p>
<div class="markdown-heading" dir="auto"><h3 tabindex="-1" class="heading-element" dir="auto"><code>to_pdf</code> Installation</h3><a id="user-content-to_pdf-installation" class="anchor" aria-label="Permalink: to_pdf Installation" href="#to_pdf-installation"><svg class="octicon octicon-link" viewBox="0 0 16 16" version="1.1" width="16" height="16" aria-hidden="true"><path d="m7.775 3.275 1.25-1.25a3.5 3.5 0 1 1 4.95 4.95l-2.5 2.5a3.5 3.5 0 0 1-4.95 0 .751.751 0 0 1 .018-1.042.751.751 0 0 1 1.042-.018 1.998 1.998 0 0 0 2.83 0l2.5-2.5a2.002 2.002 0 0 0-2.83-2.83l-1.25 1.25a.751.751 0 0 1-1.042-.018.751.751 0 0 1-.018-1.042Zm-4.69 9.64a1.998 1.998 0 0 0 2.83 0l1.25-1.25a.751.751 0 0 1 1.042.018.751.751 0 0 1 .018 1.042l-1.25 1.25a3.5 3.5 0 1 1-4.95-4.95l2.5-2.5a3.5 3.5 0 0 1 4.95 0 .751.751 0 0 1-.018 1.042.751.751 0 0 1-1.042.018 1.998 1.998 0 0 0-2.83 0l-2.5 2.5a1.998 1.998 0 0 0 0 2.83Z"></path></svg></a></div>
<p dir="auto">To install <code>to_pdf</code>, install it the same way as you install Fabric, just with a different repo name.</p>
<div class="highlight highlight-source-shell notranslate position-relative overflow-auto" dir="auto" data-snippet-clipboard-copy-content="go install github.com/danielmiessler/fabric/cmd/to_pdf@latest"><pre>go install github.com/danielmiessler/fabric/cmd/to_pdf@latest</pre></div>
<p dir="auto">Make sure you have a LaTeX distribution (like TeX Live or MiKTeX) installed on your system, as <code>to_pdf</code> requires <code>pdflatex</code> to be available in your system's PATH.</p>
<div class="markdown-heading" dir="auto"><h3 tabindex="-1" class="heading-element" dir="auto"><code>code_helper</code></h3><a id="user-content-code_helper" class="anchor" aria-label="Permalink: code_helper" href="#code_helper"><svg class="octicon octicon-link" viewBox="0 0 16 16" version="1.1" width="16" height="16" aria-hidden="true"><path d="m7.775 3.275 1.25-1.25a3.5 3.5 0 1 1 4.95 4.95l-2.5 2.5a3.5 3.5 0 0 1-4.95 0 .751.751 0 0 1 .018-1.042.751.751 0 0 1 1.042-.018 1.998 1.998 0 0 0 2.83 0l2.5-2.5a2.002 2.002 0 0 0-2.83-2.83l-1.25 1.25a.751.751 0 0 1-1.042-.018.751.751 0 0 1-.018-1.042Zm-4.69 9.64a1.998 1.998 0 0 0 2.83 0l1.25-1.25a.751.751 0 0 1 1.042.018.751.751 0 0 1 .018 1.042l-1.25 1.25a3.5 3.5 0 1 1-4.95-4.95l2.5-2.5a3.5 3.5 0 0 1 4.95 0 .751.751 0 0 1-.018 1.042.751.751 0 0 1-1.042.018 1.998 1.998 0 0 0-2.83 0l-2.5 2.5a1.998 1.998 0 0 0 0 2.83Z"></path></svg></a></div>
<p dir="auto"><code>code_helper</code> is used in conjunction with the <code>create_coding_feature</code> pattern.
It generates a <code>json</code> representation of a directory of code that can be fed into an AI model
with instructions to create a new feature or edit the code in a specified way.</p>
<p dir="auto">See <a href="/danielmiessler/Fabric/blob/main/data/patterns/create_coding_feature/README.md">the Create Coding Feature Pattern README</a> for details.</p>
<p dir="auto">Install it first using:</p>
<div class="highlight highlight-source-shell notranslate position-relative overflow-auto" dir="auto" data-snippet-clipboard-copy-content="go install github.com/danielmiessler/fabric/cmd/code_helper@latest"><pre>go install github.com/danielmiessler/fabric/cmd/code_helper@latest</pre></div>
<div class="markdown-heading" dir="auto"><h2 tabindex="-1" class="heading-element" dir="auto">pbpaste</h2><a id="user-content-pbpaste" class="anchor" aria-label="Permalink: pbpaste" href="#pbpaste"><svg class="octicon octicon-link" viewBox="0 0 16 16" version="1.1" width="16" height="16" aria-hidden="true"><path d="m7.775 3.275 1.25-1.25a3.5 3.5 0 1 1 4.95 4.95l-2.5 2.5a3.5 3.5 0 0 1-4.95 0 .751.751 0 0 1 .018-1.042.751.751 0 0 1 1.042-.018 1.998 1.998 0 0 0 2.83 0l2.5-2.5a2.002 2.002 0 0 0-2.83-2.83l-1.25 1.25a.751.751 0 0 1-1.042-.018.751.751 0 0 1-.018-1.042Zm-4.69 9.64a1.998 1.998 0 0 0 2.83 0l1.25-1.25a.751.751 0 0 1 1.042.018.751.751 0 0 1 .018 1.042l-1.25 1.25a3.5 3.5 0 1 1-4.95-4.95l2.5-2.5a3.5 3.5 0 0 1 4.95 0 .751.751 0 0 1-.018 1.042.751.751 0 0 1-1.042.018 1.998 1.998 0 0 0-2.83 0l-2.5 2.5a1.998 1.998 0 0 0 0 2.83Z"></path></svg></a></div>
<p dir="auto">The <a href="#examples">examples</a> use the macOS program <code>pbpaste</code> to paste content from the clipboard to pipe into <code>fabric</code> as the input. <code>pbpaste</code> is not available on Windows or Linux, but there are alternatives.</p>
<p dir="auto">On Windows, you can use the PowerShell command <code>Get-Clipboard</code> from a PowerShell command prompt. If you like, you can also alias it to <code>pbpaste</code>. If you are using classic PowerShell, edit the file <code>~\Documents\WindowsPowerShell\.profile.ps1</code>, or if you are using PowerShell Core, edit <code>~\Documents\PowerShell\.profile.ps1</code> and add the alias,</p>
<div class="highlight highlight-source-powershell notranslate position-relative overflow-auto" dir="auto" data-snippet-clipboard-copy-content="Set-Alias pbpaste Get-Clipboard"><pre><span class="pl-c1">Set-Alias</span> pbpaste <span class="pl-c1">Get-Clipboard</span></pre></div>
<p dir="auto">On Linux, you can use <code>xclip -selection clipboard -o</code> to paste from the clipboard. You will likely need to install <code>xclip</code> with your package manager. For Debian based systems including Ubuntu,</p>
<div class="highlight highlight-source-shell notranslate position-relative overflow-auto" dir="auto" data-snippet-clipboard-copy-content="sudo apt update
sudo apt install xclip -y"><pre>sudo apt update
sudo apt install xclip -y</pre></div>
<p dir="auto">You can also create an alias by editing <code>~/.bashrc</code> or <code>~/.zshrc</code> and adding the alias,</p>
<div class="highlight highlight-source-shell notranslate position-relative overflow-auto" dir="auto" data-snippet-clipboard-copy-content="alias pbpaste='xclip -selection clipboard -o'"><pre><span class="pl-c1">alias</span> pbpaste=<span class="pl-s"><span class="pl-pds">'</span>xclip -selection clipboard -o<span class="pl-pds">'</span></span></pre></div>
<div class="markdown-heading" dir="auto"><h2 tabindex="-1" class="heading-element" dir="auto">Web Interface</h2><a id="user-content-web-interface" class="anchor" aria-label="Permalink: Web Interface" href="#web-interface"><svg class="octicon octicon-link" viewBox="0 0 16 16" version="1.1" width="16" height="16" aria-hidden="true"><path d="m7.775 3.275 1.25-1.25a3.5 3.5 0 1 1 4.95 4.95l-2.5 2.5a3.5 3.5 0 0 1-4.95 0 .751.751 0 0 1 .018-1.042.751.751 0 0 1 1.042-.018 1.998 1.998 0 0 0 2.83 0l2.5-2.5a2.002 2.002 0 0 0-2.83-2.83l-1.25 1.25a.751.751 0 0 1-1.042-.018.751.751 0 0 1-.018-1.042Zm-4.69 9.64a1.998 1.998 0 0 0 2.83 0l1.25-1.25a.751.751 0 0 1 1.042.018.751.751 0 0 1 .018 1.042l-1.25 1.25a3.5 3.5 0 1 1-4.95-4.95l2.5-2.5a3.5 3.5 0 0 1 4.95 0 .751.751 0 0 1-.018 1.042.751.751 0 0 1-1.042.018 1.998 1.998 0 0 0-2.83 0l-2.5 2.5a1.998 1.998 0 0 0 0 2.83Z"></path></svg></a></div>
<p dir="auto">Fabric now includes a built-in web interface that provides a GUI alternative to the command-line interface and an out-of-the-box website for those who want to get started with web development or blogging.
You can use this app as a GUI interface for Fabric, a ready to go blog-site, or a website template for your own projects.</p>
<p dir="auto">The <code>web/src/lib/content</code> directory includes starter <code>.obsidian/</code> and <code>templates/</code> directories, allowing you to open up the <code>web/src/lib/content/</code> directory as an <a href="https://obsidian.md" rel="nofollow">Obsidian.md</a> vault. You can place your posts in the posts directory when you're ready to publish.</p>
<div class="markdown-heading" dir="auto"><h3 tabindex="-1" class="heading-element" dir="auto">Installing</h3><a id="user-content-installing" class="anchor" aria-label="Permalink: Installing" href="#installing"><svg class="octicon octicon-link" viewBox="0 0 16 16" version="1.1" width="16" height="16" aria-hidden="true"><path d="m7.775 3.275 1.25-1.25a3.5 3.5 0 1 1 4.95 4.95l-2.5 2.5a3.5 3.5 0 0 1-4.95 0 .751.751 0 0 1 .018-1.042.751.751 0 0 1 1.042-.018 1.998 1.998 0 0 0 2.83 0l2.5-2.5a2.002 2.002 0 0 0-2.83-2.83l-1.25 1.25a.751.751 0 0 1-1.042-.018.751.751 0 0 1-.018-1.042Zm-4.69 9.64a1.998 1.998 0 0 0 2.83 0l1.25-1.25a.751.751 0 0 1 1.042.018.751.751 0 0 1 .018 1.042l-1.25 1.25a3.5 3.5 0 1 1-4.95-4.95l2.5-2.5a3.5 3.5 0 0 1 4.95 0 .751.751 0 0 1-.018 1.042.751.751 0 0 1-1.042.018 1.998 1.998 0 0 0-2.83 0l-2.5 2.5a1.998 1.998 0 0 0 0 2.83Z"></path></svg></a></div>
<p dir="auto">The GUI can be installed by navigating to the <code>web</code> directory and using <code>npm install</code>, <code>pnpm install</code>, or your favorite package manager. Then simply run the development server to start the app.</p>
<p dir="auto"><em>You will need to run fabric in a separate terminal with the <code>fabric --serve</code> command.</em></p>
<p dir="auto"><strong>From the fabric project <code>web/</code> directory:</strong></p>
<div class="highlight highlight-source-shell notranslate position-relative overflow-auto" dir="auto" data-snippet-clipboard-copy-content="npm run dev

## or ##

pnpm run dev

## or your equivalent"><pre>npm run dev

<span class="pl-c"><span class="pl-c">#</span># or ##</span>

pnpm run dev

<span class="pl-c"><span class="pl-c">#</span># or your equivalent</span></pre></div>
<div class="markdown-heading" dir="auto"><h3 tabindex="-1" class="heading-element" dir="auto">Streamlit UI</h3><a id="user-content-streamlit-ui" class="anchor" aria-label="Permalink: Streamlit UI" href="#streamlit-ui"><svg class="octicon octicon-link" viewBox="0 0 16 16" version="1.1" width="16" height="16" aria-hidden="true"><path d="m7.775 3.275 1.25-1.25a3.5 3.5 0 1 1 4.95 4.95l-2.5 2.5a3.5 3.5 0 0 1-4.95 0 .751.751 0 0 1 .018-1.042.751.751 0 0 1 1.042-.018 1.998 1.998 0 0 0 2.83 0l2.5-2.5a2.002 2.002 0 0 0-2.83-2.83l-1.25 1.25a.751.751 0 0 1-1.042-.018.751.751 0 0 1-.018-1.042Zm-4.69 9.64a1.998 1.998 0 0 0 2.83 0l1.25-1.25a.751.751 0 0 1 1.042.018.751.751 0 0 1 .018 1.042l-1.25 1.25a3.5 3.5 0 1 1-4.95-4.95l2.5-2.5a3.5 3.5 0 0 1 4.95 0 .751.751 0 0 1-.018 1.042.751.751 0 0 1-1.042.018 1.998 1.998 0 0 0-2.83 0l-2.5 2.5a1.998 1.998 0 0 0 0 2.83Z"></path></svg></a></div>
<p dir="auto">To run the Streamlit user interface:</p>
<div class="highlight highlight-source-shell notranslate position-relative overflow-auto" dir="auto" data-snippet-clipboard-copy-content="# Install required dependencies
pip install -r requirements.txt

# Or manually install dependencies
pip install streamlit pandas matplotlib seaborn numpy python-dotenv pyperclip

# Run the Streamlit app
streamlit run streamlit.py"><pre><span class="pl-c"><span class="pl-c">#</span> Install required dependencies</span>
pip install -r requirements.txt

<span class="pl-c"><span class="pl-c">#</span> Or manually install dependencies</span>
pip install streamlit pandas matplotlib seaborn numpy python-dotenv pyperclip

<span class="pl-c"><span class="pl-c">#</span> Run the Streamlit app</span>
streamlit run streamlit.py</pre></div>
<p dir="auto">The Streamlit UI provides a user-friendly interface for:</p>
<ul dir="auto">
<li>Running and chaining patterns</li>
<li>Managing pattern outputs</li>
<li>Creating and editing patterns</li>
<li>Analyzing pattern results</li>
</ul>
<div class="markdown-heading" dir="auto"><h4 tabindex="-1" class="heading-element" dir="auto">Clipboard Support</h4><a id="user-content-clipboard-support" class="anchor" aria-label="Permalink: Clipboard Support" href="#clipboard-support"><svg class="octicon octicon-link" viewBox="0 0 16 16" version="1.1" width="16" height="16" aria-hidden="true"><path d="m7.775 3.275 1.25-1.25a3.5 3.5 0 1 1 4.95 4.95l-2.5 2.5a3.5 3.5 0 0 1-4.95 0 .751.751 0 0 1 .018-1.042.751.751 0 0 1 1.042-.018 1.998 1.998 0 0 0 2.83 0l2.5-2.5a2.002 2.002 0 0 0-2.83-2.83l-1.25 1.25a.751.751 0 0 1-1.042-.018.751.751 0 0 1-.018-1.042Zm-4.69 9.64a1.998 1.998 0 0 0 2.83 0l1.25-1.25a.751.751 0 0 1 1.042.018.751.751 0 0 1 .018 1.042l-1.25 1.25a3.5 3.5 0 1 1-4.95-4.95l2.5-2.5a3.5 3.5 0 0 1 4.95 0 .751.751 0 0 1-.018 1.042.751.751 0 0 1-1.042.018 1.998 1.998 0 0 0-2.83 0l-2.5 2.5a1.998 1.998 0 0 0 0 2.83Z"></path></svg></a></div>
<p dir="auto">The Streamlit UI supports clipboard operations across different platforms:</p>
<ul dir="auto">
<li><strong>macOS</strong>: Uses <code>pbcopy</code> and <code>pbpaste</code> (built-in)</li>
<li><strong>Windows</strong>: Uses <code>pyperclip</code> library (install with <code>pip install pyperclip</code>)</li>
<li><strong>Linux</strong>: Uses <code>xclip</code> (install with <code>sudo apt-get install xclip</code> or equivalent for your Linux distribution)</li>
</ul>
<div class="markdown-heading" dir="auto"><h2 tabindex="-1" class="heading-element" dir="auto">Meta</h2><a id="user-content-meta" class="anchor" aria-label="Permalink: Meta" href="#meta"><svg class="octicon octicon-link" viewBox="0 0 16 16" version="1.1" width="16" height="16" aria-hidden="true"><path d="m7.775 3.275 1.25-1.25a3.5 3.5 0 1 1 4.95 4.95l-2.5 2.5a3.5 3.5 0 0 1-4.95 0 .751.751 0 0 1 .018-1.042.751.751 0 0 1 1.042-.018 1.998 1.998 0 0 0 2.83 0l2.5-2.5a2.002 2.002 0 0 0-2.83-2.83l-1.25 1.25a.751.751 0 0 1-1.042-.018.751.751 0 0 1-.018-1.042Zm-4.69 9.64a1.998 1.998 0 0 0 2.83 0l1.25-1.25a.751.751 0 0 1 1.042.018.751.751 0 0 1 .018 1.042l-1.25 1.25a3.5 3.5 0 1 1-4.95-4.95l2.5-2.5a3.5 3.5 0 0 1 4.95 0 .751.751 0 0 1-.018 1.042.751.751 0 0 1-1.042.018 1.998 1.998 0 0 0-2.83 0l-2.5 2.5a1.998 1.998 0 0 0 0 2.83Z"></path></svg></a></div>
<div class="markdown-alert markdown-alert-note" dir="auto"><p class="markdown-alert-title" dir="auto"><svg class="octicon octicon-info mr-2" viewBox="0 0 16 16" version="1.1" width="16" height="16" aria-hidden="true"><path d="M0 8a8 8 0 1 1 16 0A8 8 0 0 1 0 8Zm8-6.5a6.5 6.5 0 1 0 0 13 6.5 6.5 0 0 0 0-13ZM6.5 7.75A.75.75 0 0 1 7.25 7h1a.75.75 0 0 1 .75.75v2.75h.25a.75.75 0 0 1 0 1.5h-2a.75.75 0 0 1 0-1.5h.25v-2h-.25a.75.75 0 0 1-.75-.75ZM8 6a1 1 0 1 1 0-2 1 1 0 0 1 0 2Z"></path></svg>Note</p><p dir="auto">Special thanks to the following people for their inspiration and contributions!</p>
</div>
<ul dir="auto">
<li><em>Jonathan Dunn</em> for being the absolute MVP dev on the project, including spearheading the new Go version, as well as the GUI! All this while also being a full-time medical doctor!</li>
<li><em>Caleb Sima</em> for pushing me over the edge of whether to make this a public project or not.</li>
<li><em>Eugen Eisler</em> and <em>Frederick Ros</em> for their invaluable contributions to the Go version</li>
<li><em>David Peters</em> for his work on the web interface.</li>
<li><em>Joel Parish</em> for super useful input on the project's Github directory structure..</li>
<li><em>Joseph Thacker</em> for the idea of a <code>-c</code> context flag that adds pre-created context in the <code>./config/fabric/</code> directory to all Pattern queries.</li>
<li><em>Jason Haddix</em> for the idea of a stitch (chained Pattern) to filter content using a local model before sending on to a cloud model, i.e., cleaning customer data using <code>llama2</code> before sending on to <code>gpt-4</code> for analysis.</li>
<li><em>Andre Guerra</em> for assisting with numerous components to make things simpler and more maintainable.</li>
</ul>

  <h2 class="mb-3 h4">About</h2>

      <p class="f4 my-3">
        Fabric is an open-source framework for augmenting humans using AI. It provides a modular system for solving specific problems using a crowdsourced set of AI prompts that can be used anywhere.
      </p>
      <div class="my-3 d-flex flex-items-center">
        <svg aria-hidden="true" height="16" viewBox="0 0 16 16" version="1.1" width="16" data-view-component="true" class="octicon octicon-link flex-shrink-0 mr-2">
    <path d="m7.775 3.275 1.25-1.25a3.5 3.5 0 1 1 4.95 4.95l-2.5 2.5a3.5 3.5 0 0 1-4.95 0 .751.751 0 0 1 .018-1.042.751.751 0 0 1 1.042-.018 1.998 1.998 0 0 0 2.83 0l2.5-2.5a2.002 2.002 0 0 0-2.83-2.83l-1.25 1.25a.751.751 0 0 1-1.042-.018.751.751 0 0 1-.018-1.042Zm-4.69 9.64a1.998 1.998 0 0 0 2.83 0l1.25-1.25a.751.751 0 0 1 1.042.018.751.751 0 0 1 .018 1.042l-1.25 1.25a3.5 3.5 0 1 1-4.95-4.95l2.5-2.5a3.5 3.5 0 0 1 4.95 0 .751.751 0 0 1-.018 1.042.751.751 0 0 1-1.042.018 1.998 1.998 0 0 0-2.83 0l-2.5 2.5a1.998 1.998 0 0 0 0 2.83Z"></path>
